**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. ### **Revisions Summary**

Upon review, I have refined the initial categorization to enhance clarity, reduce overlap between areas, and create a more intuitive structure for analysis. The number of primary areas has been expanded from seven to eight to allow for more precise and logical grouping of the diverse news items.

The key changes are as follows:

1.  **Creation of a Dedicated "Domestic Policy & Social Issues" Area (Area 6):** My initial structure combined Judiciary/Legal matters with Civil Rights. This has been separated. The new **Area 6** now specifically houses articles on social issues like LGBTQ and reproductive rights, the social safety net (Medicaid cuts), and domestic security/surveillance (Palantir, political violence). This prevents the "Judiciary" area from becoming a catch-all for rights-based issues and provides a clear home for major domestic policy debates that are not purely legislative or economic.

2.  **Refined "Judiciary, Law & Investigations" Area (Area 5):** With civil rights issues moved to their own area, **Area 5** is now more tightly focused on the institutions and processes of the legal system: the Supreme Court, the Department of Justice, federal investigations like the Epstein case, and legal frameworks like campaign finance.

3.  **Sharpened "Foreign Policy" and "Executive Branch" Areas (Areas 7 & 1):** The USAID shutdown story has global repercussions but is fundamentally an executive/legislative action. While its effects are international, the cause is domestic policy. I've decided the articles about the *shutdown itself* and its cost belong in Area 1 (Agency Policy), while articles about the *international consequences* (deaths, criticism from allies) belong in Area 7 (International Aid). This better reflects the cause-and-effect nature of the news.

4.  **Renaming for Clarity:** Several Area and Topic titles were slightly modified for greater precision. For example, "Public Opinion & Societal Trends" was changed to "Public Opinion & Media Narratives" to better capture articles about polling and how events are being framed. "Domestic Threats" and "Data Surveillance" were consolidated under the more descriptive "Domestic Security, Surveillance & Political Tensions."

These revisions result in a more robust and logically coherent framework that will allow for a clearer and more insightful briefing in the subsequent steps. Each article now has a more definitive "best-fit" category.

### **Daily Briefing: June 13, 2025**

**A Note for All Parties:** This briefing synthesizes raw intelligence from today's media cycle. The information is presented objectively to inform leadership of emergent situations. Analysis is strictly confined to the provided source material.

---

### **Area 1: Executive Branch: Actions & Controversies**

**Topic 1.1: The Trump-Musk Feud Escalates, Threatening Economic and Political Stability**

An intense public conflict has erupted between President Trump and his former tech czar, Elon Musk, originating from Musk's criticism of a Republican budget and tax plan [1, 2]. What began as a policy disagreement has rapidly devolved into direct threats and political maneuvering. The President has responded with escalating rhetoric, publicly suggesting he might deploy the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)—a department he has termed a "monster"—to "go back and eat Elon" [3]. President Trump explicitly linked this threat to Musk's extensive portfolio of federal subsidies, stating, "Elon may get more subsidy than any human being in history," and suggesting DOGE could be unleashed to review them [4]. The feud has sharpened to the point where, when asked directly about deporting the South African-born Musk, the President stated he would "take a look" at the possibility [5].

In response to the President's actions, Musk has reportedly vowed to financially support a "nemesis" of President Trump in future political contests and has taken the further step of publicly proposing the formation of a new political party [6, 7]. The financial markets have reacted to this instability, with one report noting that Tesla's stock "tumbled" immediately following the President's threats [8]. Musk's proposal for a new "America Party" has been met with skepticism in media commentary, with one op-ed suggesting it is "doomed" [9].

### **Area 2: Congress: Legislation & Power Debates**

**Topic 2.1: Republican Tax & Spending Bill Stalls Amid Internal Strife**

A cornerstone of the Republican legislative agenda, a massive tax and spending package termed the "big, beautiful bill," has reportedly ground "to a standstill" in the Senate amid internal party struggles [1]. Analysis of the bill's content, according to one detailed report, indicates that "businesses and higher-income households would be some of the biggest beneficiaries," with tax cuts "partly paid for with cuts to health insurance for lower-income households" [2]. Another analysis suggests the legislation is designed to push "millions of people away from the social safety net" [3]. As the bill faces a critical juncture, President Trump has personally intervened, issuing a "warning" regarding its passage while also being accused in one report of promoting a "fraudulent claim about taxes" to build support for the measure [4, 5].

A key technology provision within the broader Republican legislative package has been decisively rejected. The Senate voted 99-1 to strip an AI-related component from the President's tax bill [1]. This move coincided with the Senate also dropping a separate, but related, proposal to ban state-level AI laws, signaling a broader congressional skepticism toward sweeping federal AI regulation at this time [2, 3].

**Topic 2.3: Debates on Presidential Power and Term Limits**

Legislation and discussions with major constitutional implications are active in Congress. In the House, bill H.R.4264 has been formally introduced. Its stated purpose is to amend Title 10 of the U.S. Code to "modify the authority of the President to use the Armed Forces domestically" for the purpose of enforcing federal law [1]. Concurrently, an unnamed Republican Representative has publicly claimed there is "a lot of support" for a potential constitutional amendment that would allow President Trump to serve a third term, a direct challenge to the 22nd Amendment [2]. Senator Thom Tillis, in what one report frames as a decision to "Quit" to "Tell the Truth in Trump’s GOP Cult," appears to be dissenting against the party's current direction, though specific details of his departure are not provided [3].

### 2.3 Debates on Presidential Power and Term Limits

Legislation and discussions with major constitutional implications are active in Congress. In the House, bill H.R.4264 has been formally introduced. Its stated purpose is to amend Title 10 of the U.S. Code to "modify the authority of the President to use the Armed Forces domestically" for the purpose of enforcing federal law [1]. Concurrently, an unnamed Republican Representative has publicly claimed there is "a lot of support" for a potential constitutional amendment that would allow President Trump to serve a third term, a direct challenge to the 22nd Amendment [2]. Senator Thom Tillis, in what one report frames as a decision to "Quit" to "Tell the Truth in Trump’s GOP Cult," appears to be dissenting against the party's current direction, though specific details of his departure are not provided [3].

**Citations:**  
[1] H.R.4264 - To amend title 10, United States Code, to modify the authority of the President to use the Armed Forces domestically to enforce Federal authority and to address interference with State and Federal law., https://www.congress.gov/bill/119th-congress/house-bill/4264?q=%7B%22search%22%3A%22congressId%3A119+AND+billStatus%3A%5C%22Introduced%5C%22%22%7D&s=1&r=7  
[2] Amendment to Give Trump a Third Term Has 'A Lot of Support': GOP Rep, https://www.newsweek.com/donald-trump-third-term-amendment-andy-ogles-republican-support-2078812  
[3] Thom Tillis Figured Out How to Tell the Truth in Trump’s GOP Cult: Quit, https://www.thenation.com/article/politics/thom-tillis-big-beautiful-bill-trump/

## 3. Immigration, Citizenship & Border Control

### 3.1 New Citizenship Bans and Intensified Enforcement

The administration is moving forward with significant policy shifts regarding citizenship and enforcement. A reported ban on birthright citizenship from the administration is expected to have a tangible impact across all 50 states on July 27, with Social Security offices reportedly bracing for fallout from an anticipated ruling [1, 2]. In parallel, one headline indicates the Department of Justice is prioritizing "denaturalization"—the process of revoking citizenship—raising constitutional questions [3]. This push is coupled with an intensified enforcement strategy, involving "mass deportations" built through "global deal-making" [4]. These actions are creating domestic economic consequences, as immigration raids in California have reportedly left crops unharvested and placed farms at financial risk [5].

**Citations:**  
[1] How Trump's birthright citizenship ban could impact all 50 states on July 27, https://www.kuow.org/stories/what-the-birthright-citizenship-ban-means-for-washington-state

### 3.2 'Alligator Alcatraz' Detention Facility Opens Amid Protest

A controversial immigrant detention facility in Florida, publicly dubbed "Alligator Alcatraz," is set to open this week with President Trump scheduled to be in attendance [1]. Its opening has been met with organized protests from activist groups citing both humanitarian and environmental grounds. The facility is also seen as a "political boost" for Florida Governor Ron DeSantis [2]. The President's commentary has fueled the controversy, particularly his remark that migrants would need to know "how to run away from an alligator" to escape, a statement one outlet suggests "will stir dark echoes" [3, 4].

## 4. Foreign Policy, Domestic Security & Judiciary

### 4.1 Fallout from USAID Shutdown and Middle East Tensions

The administration's decision to gut the U.S. Agency for International Development (USAID) is drawing stark warnings and high-profile rebukes. A study cited in one report warns that eliminating the agency's programs may lead to an additional 14 million deaths globally over the next five years [1]. On the agency's final day of operation, former Presidents George W. Bush and Barack Obama, along with the singer Bono, publicly faulted President Trump for the policy [2]. Separately, tensions in the Middle East remain high. A group of 19 U.S. lawmakers led by Rep. Rashida Tlaib is publicly demanding that Israel cease actions described as "starving Gaza" [3]. Domestically, public anxiety is elevated, with a poll indicating that three in four Americans worry about potential retaliation from Iran following recent U.S. strikes [4].

[1] USAID cuts may cause 14 million more deaths in next five years, study says, https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2025/07/01/usaid-cuts-aid-14-million-deaths/?utm_campaign=wp_main&utm_source=twitter&utm_medium=social  
[2] Bush, Obama — and singer Bono — fault Trump's gutting of USAID on agency's last day, https://apnews.com/article/obama-bono-bush-usaid-trump-950f7708c01502c759f1c10524752b8e

### 4.2 Domestic Security Concerns and Judicial Developments

Reports are highlighting growing concerns about domestic surveillance and the potential for political violence. One analysis warns that Peter Thiel's data company, Palantir, through its work with the Trump administration, "poses a grave threat" and could potentially be used to target the president's political opponents [1]. This is amplified by another report pointing to a segment of the population described as "White, legally armed, and primed for political violence" [2]. In the judicial sphere, a mystery now surrounds the Jeffrey Epstein case following claims by Attorney General Pam Bondi of "tens of thousands" of pieces of evidence, including videos, though no further details have been made public [3]. Concurrently, recent commentary suggests the Supreme Court's orientation is shifting, with one op-ed arguing "The Supreme Court Isn’t Interested In Stopping Trump" [4].

## 5. Economic & Domestic Policy

### 5.1 Economic Policy Impacts: Interest Rates and Energy Sector

Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell has explicitly connected the administration's tariff policies to monetary decisions. In recent public statements, Chair Powell confirmed that interest rate cuts have been held up, stating the Fed "would have cut by now" if not for the tariffs imposed by President Trump [1, 2]. The proposed Republican budget is also projected to have a severe impact on specific sectors, with one analysis concluding the bill is "poised to crush renewable energy in the US" by eliminating clean-energy tax credits while simultaneously encouraging new oil drilling [3].

**Citations:**  
[1] Powell confirms that the Fed would have cut by now were it not for tariffs, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/01/powell-confirms-that-the-fed-would-have-cut-by-now-were-it-not-for-tariffs.html  
[2] Powell: Trump’s tariffs held up rate cuts, https://thehill.com/business/5378903-fed-chair-powell-tariffs-rate-cuts/  
[3] GOP budget bill poised to crush renewable energy in the US | Say goodbye to clean-energy tax credits, hello to new oil wells., https://arstechnica.com/tech-policy/2025/07/gop-budget-bill-poised-to-crush-renewable-energy-in-the-us  

### 5.2 Cuts to Social Safety Net and Public Services

The administration is taking direct action impacting bedrock social programs. Federal education funds amounting to a reported $6.8 billion have been frozen, a move that has "hit California hard" [1]. Separately, Vice President JD Vance has drawn sharp criticism for dismissing the impact of millions of Americans losing Medicaid as "minutiae." Rep. Ro Khanna was quoted in a headline questioning the Vice President's stance and noting, "Medicaid cuts... will close rural hospitals and kick millions off healthcare" [2]. These actions are occurring as the Republican spending bill is being characterized in one headline as a "disaster for reproductive rights" and a ProPublica investigation found that after Texas banned abortion, there was a "striking" trend of more women nearly bleeding to death during miscarriage [3, 4].
